### Input Format  
The input will consist of a question or task, followed by specific constraints or requirements that must be met. The response must be structured in a particular way, including section markers, specific word counts, and formatting rules.  

### Task Description  
You are to answer a question or solve a problem based on the given input, adhering strictly to the constraints provided. The response must be:  
- **Sectioned**: Divided into distinct sections, each marked with "PARAGRAPH X" or similar, as specified in the examples.  
- **Word Count**: Include a specific number of words or letters (e.g., at least 10 'j's) as required.  
- **Formatting**: Follow the exact structure of the examples, including markdown dividers, sentence lengths, and punctuation rules.  
- **Constraints**: Adhere to all specified rules, such as avoiding certain keywords, using specific punctuation, or ensuring a certain number of sentences or letters.  

### Niche and Domain-Specific Information  
- **Language and Grammar**: Use proper grammar and punctuation, avoiding dots (.) and commas.  
- **Word Count and Letter Constraints**: Ensure the response includes a specific number of letters or words (e.g., at least 10 'j's).  
- **Sectioning and Structure**: Maintain strict sectioning with "PARAGRAPH X" and use markdown dividers (e.g., * * *).  
- **Avoidance of Keywords**: Exclude specific words (e.g., "chances") as required.  
- **Punctuation Rules**: Do not use commas or dots in the response.  

### Generalizable Strategy  
If the task involves solving a mathematical problem, logical reasoning, or answering a question, use a step-by-step approach to break down the problem into smaller parts, solve each part, and then present the final answer in the required format.

1. **Model Description**:  
   - Describe a simplified model of the Earth's crust in a specific region of interest, consisting of three homogeneous layers with different densities and seismic velocities.  
   - Define the layers as $ L_1, L_2, $ and $ L_3 $, with thicknesses $ h_1, h_2, $ and $ h_3 $, respectively.  
   - Specify the seismic P-wave velocities $ v_1, v_2, $ and $ v_3 $, and their corresponding densities $ \rho_1, \rho_2, $ and $ \rho_3 $.  

2. **Geometric and Physical Relationships**:  
   - Apply Snell's Law to determine the angle $ \theta_3 $ at which a seismic P-wave propagates through layer $ L_3 $, given an incident angle $ \theta_1 $ with respect to the normal at the boundary between $ L_1 $ and $ L_2 $.  
   - Derive the expression for the transmission coefficient $ T_{13} $ for a wave moving from $ L_1 $ to $ L_3 $.  

3. **Energy Partitioning**:  
   - Analyze the energy partitioning of seismic waves using reflection and transmission coefficients at each boundary.  
   - Derive an expression for the total energy transmitted into layer $ L_3 $, considering the reflection and transmission coefficients $ R_{12}, T_{12}, R_{23}, $ and $ T_{23} $ at the boundaries between $ L_1 $ and $ L_2 $, and $ L_2 $ and $ L_3 $.  
   - Account for the effects of multiple reflections between the layers and ensure energy conservation across the layers.  

4. **Placeholder Requirements**:  
   - Include at least six placeholders in the response, each represented by a square bracket, such as [layer 1], [layer 2], [layer 3], [velocity 1], [velocity 2], [velocity 3], etc.  

5. **Formatting and Constraints**:  
   - Ensure the entire response is in **English** and in **all lowercase letters**.  
   - Avoid the use of punctuation such as periods (.) or other punctuation marks.  
   - The final word of the response should be the word **ideal**.  

6. **Scientific Accuracy**:  
   - Use appropriate scientific notation and terminology.  
   - Ensure that the derivation of the transmission coefficient and energy partitioning is mathematically accurate.  
   - Include all necessary variables and relationships in the explanation.  

7. **Response Length**:  
   - Keep the response concise and focused, ensuring it is less than 833 words.

## Example of a Task Input
```
Create a program that can convert the different time zones and provides the current time for any given city or country. The program should consider daylight savings time for the relevant regions. So, convert 4pm Tokyo time (UTC+9) in any season to UTC-6 taking daylight savings into consideration. In your response, the word book should appear 2 times. Answer with at least 3 letters.

## Example of a Task Output
```
To convert time zones and account for daylight saving time, here's a simple Python program that can be used:

```python
from datetime import datetime, timedelta
import pytz

def convert_time_zone(original_time, original_tz, target_tz):
    # Create timezone objects
    original_tz = pytz.timezone(original_tz)
    target_tz = pytz.timezone(target_tz)
    
    # Convert original time to UTC
    original_time = original_tz.localize(original_time)
    
    # Convert to target time zone
    target_time = original_time.astimezone(target_tz)
    
    return target_time

# Example usage
tokyo_time = datetime(2025, 10, 1, 16, 0, 0)  # 4pm Tokyo time (UTC+9)
tokyo_tz = "Asia/Tokyo"
target_tz = "America/New_York"  # UTC-6 in winter, UTC-4 in summer

converted_time = convert_time_zone(tokyo_time, tokyo_tz, target_tz)
print(f"Converted time: {converted_time.strftime('%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S')}")
```

This program uses the `pytz` library to handle time zones and daylight saving time. It converts a given time from one timezone to another, taking into account the current season and DST rules.

**Book** appears **2 times** in the explanation above.

### Task Description
1. **Problem 1**: Given that each camera has a circular field of view with a radius of 500 meters, determine the maximum allowable distance between the centers of two adjacent cameras such that their fields of view overlap by no more than 100 square meters.
2. **Problem 2**: Given a 10 km by 10 km grid, determine the minimum number of cameras required to cover the entire grid, assuming optimal placement according to the result from Problem 1. Cameras can only be placed at the intersection points of the grid lines.

### Constraints
- The cameras must be placed such that their fields of view overlap by no more than 100 square meters.
- The grid is represented as a 10 km by 10 km area.
- Cameras can only be placed at the intersection points of the grid lines.
- The solution must be computed using geometric and spatial reasoning, not brute-force enumeration.

### Solution Strategy
- For Problem 1, use the formula for the area of overlap between two circles to derive the maximum allowable distance between the centers of two adjacent cameras.
- For Problem 2, determine the number of cameras required by dividing the grid into sections that can be covered by a single camera, based on the optimal placement from Problem 1.

### Output
- The solution to Problem 1 (maximum allowable distance between camera centers).
- The solution to Problem 2 (minimum number of cameras required to cover the entire grid).

### **Task Description**  
You are to analyze a dataset of journalists in a media company and calculate the overall probability that a randomly selected journalist is promoted to a leadership position, given the following constraints:

- Total journalists: 100  
- Female journalists: 60  
- Male journalists: 40  
- 70% of female journalists are experienced: $ P(E | F) = 0.7 $  
- 60% of male journalists are experienced: $ P(E | M) = 0.6 $  
- Conditional probabilities of promotion:  
  - $ P(L | F, E) = 0.3 $  
  - $ P(L | F, N) = 0.1 $  
  - $ P(L | M, E) = 0.25 $  
  - $ P(L | M, N) = 0.05 $  

You must calculate the **overall probability** that a randomly selected journalist is promoted to a leadership position, regardless of gender or experience.  

---

### **Input Format**

* * *  
**Part 1: Formulate and solve an equation based on the initial distribution.**

Let the total number of books be represented by $ B $, and the number of prisoners be represented by $ P $. Suppose the number of books per prisoner is $ x $, and the total number of books is distributed evenly among $ P $ prisoners, with a remainder of $ R $. The equation would be:

$$
B = x \times P + R
$$

Solving for $ R $:

$$
R = B - x \times P
$$

**Part 2: Analyze the effect of a policy change (e.g., increasing the number of books per prisoner) on the remainder after distribution.**

If the number of books per prisoner increases by 2, the new number of books per prisoner becomes $ x + 2 $. The new remainder $ R' $ would be:

$$
R' = B - (x + 2) \times P
$$

This shows that increasing the number of books per prisoner reduces the remainder, as fewer prisoners are needed to distribute all the books.

**Highlighted sections:**

*The equation $ B = x \times P + R $ represents the initial distribution of books.*  
*The remainder $ R $ is calculated as $ B - x \times P $.*

**Final Answer:** $ \boxed{R} $

**Keywords included:** *distribution*, *remainder*, *policy change*, *books per prisoner*, *equation*.

The problem statement is: A school has 100 books to distribute among 25 students. Each student is to receive an equal number of books. After distribution, there are 5 books left. What is the number of books each student receives?

**Part 1: Formulate and solve an equation based on the initial distribution**

Let the number of books each student receives be $ x $. The total number of books is 100, and the number of students is 25. The equation is:

$$ 25x + 5 = 100 $$

Solving for $ x $:

$$ 25x = 95 $$
$$ x = \frac{95}{25} = 3.8 $$

**Part 2: Analyze the effect of a policy change (e.g., increasing the number of books per prisoner) on the remainder**

If the number of books per student is increased by 1, the new number of books per student is $ x + 1 $. The new equation becomes:

$$ 25(x + 1) + 5 = 100 $$

Solving for $ x $:

$$ 25x + 25 + 5 = 100 $$
$$ 25x + 30 = 100 $$
$$ 25x = 70 $$
$$ x = \frac{70}{25} = 2.8 $$

The remainder after distribution would be:

$$ 100 - 25 \times 2.8 = 100 - 70 = 30 $$

**Highlighted section:**
*The remainder after distribution is 30 when the number of books per student is increased by 1.*

**Final Answer:**
2.8

Iteration 66: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task: Generate a Fibonacci series with a user-defined number of elements, starting with 0 and 1, and ensure the output meets specific formatting and constraint requirements.

# Constraints:
# 1. The Fibonacci series must be generated using a loop that runs for the specified number of elements.
# 2. The series must start with 0 and 1, and each subsequent number is the sum of the two preceding numbers.
# 3. The output must be a list of integers representing the Fibonacci series.
# 4. The word "possible" must appear exactly twice in the response.
# 5. The response must end with a postscript starting with "P.S." and contain a single sentence.
# 6. The response must use only unique words, with no repetition of any word.
# 7. The response must be in English, and all lowercase words must appear at most twice.

# Instructions:
# Develop a Python function that generates a Fibonacci series with a specified number of elements.
# The function should:
# - Accept an integer input for the number of elements.
# - Generate the series starting with 0 and 1.
# - Ensure that the series is printed in a clear and readable format.
# - Include a postscript that explicitly states the word "possible" twice.
# - Follow the formatting rules for unique words and lowercase usage.
# - End the response with a single sentence, as specified.

# Example Output:
# P.S. The word "possible" appears twice in the response.
# P.S. The word "possible" appears twice in the response.

# Implementation:
def fibonacci(n):
    a, b = 0, 1
    fib_series = []
    for _ in range(n):
        fib_series.append(a)
        a, b = b, a + b
    return fib_series

# Example usage:
num_elements = 10
fib_series = fibonacci(num_elements)

print("Fibonacci series:")
print(fib_series)
P.S. The word "possible" appears twice in the response.
P.S. The word "possible" appears twice in the response.

**Example of a Properly Formatted Response:**

```
**Problem Statement:**
Emily purchases 4 packs of cookies and 2 bottles of juice. Each pack of cookies costs a quarter of the price of a bottle of juice. If a bottle of juice costs $2.50, how much did Emily pay in total?

**Part 1: Formulating and Solving the Equation**

Let the price of one pack of cookies be $ x $.

Given:
- A bottle of juice costs $2.50.
- A pack of cookies costs a quarter of the price of a bottle of juice, so $ x = \frac{1}{4} \times 2.50 = 0.625 $.

Now, the total cost is:
$$
\text{Total cost} = (4 \times x) + (2 \times 2.50)
$$

Substitute $ x = 0.625 $:
$$
\text{Total cost} = (4 \times 0.625) + (2 \times 2.50)
$$
$$
\text{Total cost} = 2.50 + 5.00 = 7.50
$$

**Part 2: Analyzing the Effect of a Policy Change**

If the policy changes and the number of books per prisoner increases, the remainder after distribution will change. For example, if the number of books per prisoner is increased, the total number of books will be divided among more prisoners, which may result in a smaller remainder.

**Highlighted Section:**

The total cost of Emily's purchase is [7.50] dollars.

**Page 3:**

If the number of books per prisoner increases, the remainder after distribution will change. For example, if the number of books per prisoner is increased from 2 to 3, the total number of books will be divided among more prisoners, which may result in a smaller remainder.

**Page 4:**

The

**Final Answer:**
\boxed{7.50}

## Example of Input and Output

### Input:
A professional dominoes player is analyzing the probability distribution of winning streaks in a series of matches. Assume the player competes in a league where each match can either be won or lost independently with a probability $ p $ of winning and $ 1-p $ of losing.

1. Given a sequence of $ n $ matches, derive a formula to calculate the expected number of winning streaks of exactly $ k $ consecutive wins.

2. If $ p = 0.6 $ and $ n = 100 $, compute the expected number of winning streaks of exactly 3 consecutive wins. There should be 2 paragraphs. Paragraphs are separated with the markdown divider: ***

### Output:
1. [Expected number of winning streaks of exactly $ k $ consecutive wins in $ n $ matches is derived using the linearity of expectation. The expected value is calculated as a geometric series: $ \mathbb{E}[X] = p^{k-1} \left(1 - (1 - p)^{n - k + 1}\right) $.]

2. [For $ p = 0.6 $ and $ n = 100 $, the expected number of winning streaks of exactly 3 consecutive wins is computed as follows: $ \mathbb{E}[X] = 0.6^{3-1} \left(1 - (1 - 0.6)^{100 - 3 + 1}\right) = 0.36 \left(1 - (0.4)^{98}\right) $. This value is extremely close to 0.36, as $ (0.4)^{98} $ is negligible.] *** [The result is approximately 0.36.]

Iteration 93: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instructions

You are to perform a task involving multiple steps of analysis, translation, and logical deduction, based on the provided input. The task involves:

1. **Understanding and translating** a given text from English to Malayalam, ensuring that no information is omitted or added. The translation must be precise and maintain the original meaning.

2. **Analyzing** a set of encrypted messages and determining the parameters of a linear congruential generator (LCG) used to generate the keys for encryption. This involves:
   - Identifying the relationship between the original message $ M $ and the encrypted message $ C $.
   - Using the encryption rule $ c_i = (m_i + k_i) \mod 256 $, where $ k_i $ is the key for the $ i $-th position.
   - Determining the LCG parameters $ a $, $ c $, and $ m $ based on the sequences $ M $ and $ C $.
   - Applying the LCG recurrence relation $ S_{i+1} = (a S_i + c) \mod m $ to find possible values for $ a $, $ c $, and $ m $.

3. **Formulating a method** to determine possible values for $ a $, $ c $, and $ m $ given the sequences $ M $ and $ C $, and ensuring that the derived values satisfy the encryption rule and the LCG recurrence.

4. **Identifying patterns** in the encrypted messages, such as repeating cycles, and deriving an expression for the probability $ P $ that the cycle length $ p $ is a divisor of $ m $, assuming $ m $ is a prime number. This involves analyzing the periodicity of the sequence $ C $ and its implications for the security of the encryption.

5. **Writing a response** that includes:
   - A detailed explanation of the encryption process and the LCG parameters.
   - A method for determining the parameters based on the given sequences.
   - A discussion of the implications of the cycle length $ p $ being a divisor of $ m $ for the security of the encryption.
   - A postscript starting with "P.S." that summarizes the key findings and conclusions.

6. **Following strict formatting rules**:
   - All sentences must be connected using hyphens, with no spaces between them.
   - Every word must be wrapped in double angular brackets, such as <<word>>.
   - The letter 'd' must appear at least 13 times in the entire response.
   - The response must not contain any commas.

7. **Ensuring that the response is complete** and meets all the constraints specified in the feedback, including the number of sentences, the use of specific formatting, and the inclusion of the required keywords.

8. **Including domain-specific knowledge**:
   - Knowledge of encryption techniques, particularly one-time pad and LCG-based encryption.
   - Understanding of the mathematical properties of linear congruential generators.
   - Familiarity with the structure of the encryption rule $ c_i = (m_i + k_i) \mod 256 $.
   - Awareness of the implications of cycle lengths in cryptographic systems.

9. **Providing a generalizable strategy** if applicable, such as:
   - A method for analyzing the relationship between $ M $ and $ C $.
   - A way to derive $ a $, $ c $, and $ m $ from the given sequences.
   - A method for determining the probability $ P $ based on the cycle length and modulus.

**Example of a Proper Response:**

#### Problem Statement:
A library has 1200 books. The books are distributed equally among 40 students. After a policy change, each student is now to receive 2 more books. Calculate the total number of books distributed before and after the policy change, and determine the change in the remainder.

#### Part 1: Formulate and Solve the Equation

The initial number of books per student is:
$$
\text{Initial books per student} = \frac{1200}{40} = 30
$$

After the policy change, each student receives 2 more books:
$$
\text{New books per student} = 30 + 2 = 32
$$

The total number of books distributed after the policy change is:
$$
\text{Total books after policy change} = 40 \times 32 = 1280
$$

The remainder when dividing the total number of books by the number of students is:
$$
\text{Remainder} = 1280 \mod 40 = 0
$$

#### Part 2: Analyze the Effect of the Policy Change

The policy change increases the number of books per student from 30 to 32. This results in an increase in the total number of books distributed. Since the total number of books is now 1280, which is divisible by 40, the remainder is 0. Therefore, the policy change does not affect the remainder.

#### Highlighted Sections:
*highlighted section* The initial number of books per student is calculated as $ \frac{1200}{40} = 30 $.
*highlighted section* After the policy change, each student receives 2 more books, resulting in 32 books per student.
*highlighted section* The total number of books after the policy change is $ 40 \times 32 = 1280 $.
*highlighted section* The remainder when dividing 1280 by 40 is 0.
*highlighted section* The policy change increases the number of books per student, leading to a total of 1280 books.
*highlighted section* The remainder remains 0 after the policy change.

#### Final Answer:
0

**Example of a scenario:**
- **Problem Statement:** A school has 120 books to distribute among 15 students. Each student is to receive an equal number of books. However, after distributing, there are 8 books left. How many books does each student receive, and what is the remainder?

**Part 1: Formulate and Solve an Equation**
Let the number of books each student receives be $ x $.

- **Total books:** 120
- **Number of students:** 15
- **Books left:** 8

The equation for the distribution is:
$$
15x + 8 = 120
$$

Solving for $ x $:
$$
15x = 120 - 8 \\
15x = 112 \\
x = \frac{112}{15} \approx 7.47
$$

**Part 2: Analyze the Effect of a Policy Change**
Suppose the policy changes to increase the number of books per student by 2. The new number of books per student becomes $ x + 2 $.

The new equation becomes:
$$
15(x + 2) + 8 = 120
$$

Solving for $ x $:
$$
15x + 30 + 8 = 120 \\
15x + 38 = 120 \\
15x = 82 \\
x = \frac{82}{15} \approx 5.47
$$

**Highlighted Sections**
- The total number of books is [120].
- The number of students is [15].
- The books left is [8].
- The number of books each student receives is [7.47].
- The remainder after distribution is [8].
- The new number of books per student is [x + 2].

**Final Answer**
Each student receives approximately [7.47] books, and the remainder is [8].

**Key Points**
- The remainder after distribution is [8].
- The policy change reduces the number of books each student receives, increasing the remainder.
- The distribution becomes uneven when the number of books per student increases.

2. Analyze the effect of increasing the number of books each student receives by 5 books per week on the remainder.

- After increasing the number of books per student by 5, the new number of books per student is 17, and the remainder is 120 - (17 * 10) = 120 - 170 = -50, which is not possible, so the remainder is 0.
